    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText1352392372654089242" style="display:none">We are shaped by our thoughts; we become what we think. When the mind is pure, joy follows like a shadow that never leaves. -Buddha <br /><br />You can achieve anything you want if you have control over your thoughts. You can replicate the life of a winner in you or you can be your enemy. It solely depends on which staircase you select for yourself; a positive value staircase or a negative value staircase. <br /><br />-Understand the art of climbing a positive value staircase and redirect your vision with the help of visualization technique. <br />-Understand when hard work leads to failure. <br />-Understand the GOAL of a goal. <br />-Understand when expectations don't hurt you. Understand the purpose of your life.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);

<div id="review_2725047926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2725047926" />
    <a title="Booxoul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80600969-booxoul"><img alt="Booxoul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566630604p2/80600969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2725047926?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Booxoul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Booxoul" href="/user/show/80600969-booxoul">Booxoul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2725047926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4834034072205554527">I am a true believer of “What we think we become”.  This theory/concept is known since eternity and hundreds of books are written, documentaries & movies are made around it, but seeing an Indian author writing a short and concise book caught my attention.<br/><br/>It started with a high but ended with a series of disappointments. The author who has already published two books had really good content for his third book but screwed up badly with his language and storytelling. His language is raw and the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText4834034072205554527" style="display:none">I am a true believer of “What we think we become”.  This theory/concept is known since eternity and hundreds of books are written, documentaries &amp; movies are made around it, but seeing an Indian author writing a short and concise book caught my attention.<br /><br />It started with a high but ended with a series of disappointments. The author who has already published two books had really good content for his third book but screwed up badly with his language and storytelling. His language is raw and the book is full of grammatical mistakes. His sentence formations are horrible. Actually, it’s not his fault, being Indian we grow up learning multiple languages but fail to master one. So, when it comes to documenting our thoughts in English, which is not our 1st language, we end up translating our emotions/ thoughts word to word losing the context.<br /><br />For instance, my mother tongue is Bengali, but I was raised in a Hindi(language) dominated state &amp; currently living in a state where Marathi is the native language. Many times, I end up forming sentences which sound correct in my mind (which mostly thinks in Hindi or Bengali) but are grammatically wrong in English.<br /><br />So back to the book, I really liked the way he has created his Index (mentioned as content). It gives you a gist of the chapter before you start reading. Chapters are short &amp; crisp with proper diagrams &amp; graphics making it easy for a reader to understand. He has also covered psychometric assessments &amp; vision boards which are useful. His “Pause &amp; Pounder” section at the end of each chapter is also very thoughtful. However, examples &amp; plots are irrelevant &amp; seem out of context.<br /><br />I appreciate his effort &amp; what he is trying to do with his “writing to serve humanity” but his writing needs a good editor. An editor who can transform his thoughts &amp; content into a good read.<br /><br />It’s a 2 star for me out of 5, just for the topic &amp; content he picked.<br /><br />My Rating: 2/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="4834034072205554527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15520520836191602064" style="display:none">Good for one time read. The book don't offer instant boosts. It talkes about a strategy to approach our success. It also talks about kind of people we meet, how our thoughts and attitude move things for us, etc. But something was lacking that instant motivation creations in us.<br />The ideas and concept was good. But i felt it like a more economics book than a self help book. As the author said in the book, " no one can motivate you if they are not of the type that actually you are interested in "<br />It didn't impress me with full effect as it's not my genre. I'm more into aderline boost supplying self help books. It may surely work for some other person. Author has done great researches and brought good points and conventional idea. You'll surely like the book if you're interested in graphs, statistics, economic kind of approaches.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lqUIHv9H8h14kHzLVqk1mc1g+eX9t59uGCU+NUUUr2gCX1ONMt9hsurkigOlhMnkR9ykBKTnnfu8cLq42yNOIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('09CXCmNNMZor4eL0UqTsHJsioTheknrPaRhjdh88DIJHKsyZrtWiNbmVFDyhiRBhEZ782QfCeFrNTef7gQvtyw==')})
  }

In bestselling author Walter <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10550039457022438127\" style=\"display:none\">Benjamin Franklin is the Founding Father who winks at us. An ambitious urban entrepreneur who rose up the social ladder, from leather-aproned shopkeeper to dining with kings, he seems made of flesh rather than of marble. In bestselling author Walter Isaacson\'s vivid and witty full-scale biography, we discover why Franklin seems to turn to us from history\'s stage with eyes that twinkle from behind his new-fangled spectacles. By bringing Franklin to life, Isaacson shows how he helped to define both his own time and ours.\n\nHe was, during his 84-year life, America\'s best scientist, inventor, diplomat, writer, and business strategist, and he was also one of its most practical—though not most profound—political thinkers. He proved by flying a kite that lightning was electricity, and he invented a rod to tame it. He sought practical ways to make stoves less smoky and commonwealths less corrupt. He organized neighborhood constabularies and international alliances, local lending libraries and national legislatures. He combined two types of lenses to create bifocals and two concepts of representation to foster the nation\'s federal compromise. He was the only man who shaped all the founding documents of America: the Albany Plan of Union, the Declaration of Independence, the treaty of alliance with France, the peace treaty with England, and the Constitution. And he helped invent America\'s unique style of homespun humor, democratic values, and philosophical pragmatism.\n\nBut the most interesting thing that Franklin invented, and continually reinvented, was himself. America\'s first great publicist, he was, in his life and in his writings, consciously trying to create a new American archetype. In the process, he carefully crafted his own persona, portrayed it in public, and polished it for posterity.\n\nThrough it all, he trusted the hearts and minds of his fellow &quot;leather-aprons&quot; more than he did those of any inbred elite. He saw middle-class values as a source of social strength, not as something to be derided. His guiding principle was a &quot;dislike of everything that tended to debase the spirit of the common people.&quot; Few of his fellow founders felt this comfort with democracy so fully, and none so intuitively.\n\nIn this colorful and intimate narrative, Isaacson provides the full sweep of Franklin\'s amazing life, from his days as a runaway printer to his triumphs as a statesman, scientist, and Founding Father. He chronicles Franklin\'s tumultuous relationship with his illegitimate son and grandson, his practical marriage, and his flirtations with the ladies of Paris. He also shows how Franklin helped to create the American character and why he has a particular resonance in the twenty-first century.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10550039457022438127\" href=\"#\" <span id="freeTextContainer13736769621225657966">Durgesh Satpathy is an author, management consultant, and an academician. He has done MBA from Nagpur University and PG Diploma in Psychological Counseling from Madurai Kamaraj University. He aims to reform the mindsets of people through his writing.<br/><br/>He is also a psychological counselor and mentor to students.
